  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b67b7460-517a-4cd7-97a8-13940fb5d9af'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer6102895003696696092">From the Flap:<br/><br/>The Master at his scarifying best! From heart-pounding terror to the eeriest of whimsy--tales from the outer limits of one of the greatest imaginations of our time!<br/><br/>Evil that breathes and walks and shrieks, brave new worlds and horror shows, human desperation bursting into deadly menace--such are the themes of these astounding works of fiction. In the traditio</span>
  <span id="freeText6102895003696696092" style="display:none">From the Flap:<br /><br />The Master at his scarifying best! From heart-pounding terror to the eeriest of whimsy--tales from the outer limits of one of the greatest imaginations of our time!<br /><br />Evil that breathes and walks and shrieks, brave new worlds and horror shows, human desperation bursting into deadly menace--such are the themes of these astounding works of fiction. In the tradition of Poe and Stevenson, of Lovecraft and The Twilight Zone, Stephen King has fused images of fear as old as time with the iconography of contemporary American life to create his own special brand of horror--one that has kept millions of readers turning the pages even as they gasp.<br /><br />In the book-length story "The Mist," a supermarket becomes the last bastion of humanity as a peril beyond dimension invades the earth. . .<br /><br />Touch "The Man Who Would Not Shake Hands," and say your prayers . . .<br /><br />There are some things in attics which are better left alone, things like "The Monkey" . . .<br /><br />The most sublime woman driver on earth offers a man "Mrs. Todd's Shortcut" to paradise . . .<br /><br />A boy's sanity is pushed to the edge when he's left alone with the odious corpse of "Gramma" . . .<br /><br />If you were stunned by Gremlins, the Fornits of "The Ballad of the Flexible Bullet" will knock your socks off . . .<br /><br />Trucks that punish and beautiful teen demons who seduce a young man to massacre; curses whose malevolence grows through the years; obscene presences and angels of grace--here, indeed, is a night-blooming bouquet of chills and thrills.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=king-stephen">king-stephen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320514528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4073404196337959743">I love his short stories, although the quality and style are varying, best to see when comparing publication date with probable intoxication. <br/><br/>The strange thing is, that there isn´t always the correlation of drug induced boo or jay and therefore the quality of the work, it´s more a result of King´s working method of letting the characters and his subconsciousness tell the story. This can go luckily well, average, or, rare exception and seen with pink fanboy goggles, average average, because there</span>
  <span id="freeText4073404196337959743" style="display:none">I love his short stories, although the quality and style are varying, best to see when comparing publication date with probable intoxication. <br /><br />The strange thing is, that there isn´t always the correlation of drug induced boo or jay and therefore the quality of the work, it´s more a result of King´s working method of letting the characters and his subconsciousness tell the story. This can go luckily well, average, or, rare exception and seen with pink fanboy goggles, average average, because there exists no bad in King´s work, ok?. Possibly, some really aren´t that great, maybe the ones the wrote in ultra stoned blackouts and can´t remember like the whole novel Cujo.<br /><br />I have to sometimes also think about the family guy episode and the potentially true grain of überproductivity in it. <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tMZONL8x8NE">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tMZON...</a><br />This could play in here too a little. <br /><br />But seriously (of course not), I want to reread it and check the publication date before because there is this timeless debate about stoned inspiration, ingenuity, and creativity, and some of King's books were made when he was a multi drug using alcoholic, so… if you want to be successful. No, really, I am so looking towards reading all of his works and compare the pre drug era, the drug era, and the later periods and dissect what makes the difference. <br /><br />I´ve read most of King´s short story collections and wouldn´t suggest beginning with this one, better take one of the later works where he was a sober, super professional, and talented writing prodigy. <br /><br />If you are a picky reader, I would suggest checking the single ratings of the reviewers who are so ambitious to rate every single short story and thereby extract the best of the best, I honestly can´t remember which one´s were the most disturbing and mind penetrating, because I read it a while ago. Except „Survivor type“, because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[hard drugs and autocannibalism <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> are an always perfect match made in hell. Yum, now I want to have a special snack and some mind altering substances. <br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/SkeletonCrew">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3552209997" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3552209997" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1232712-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552603488p2/1232712.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3552209997?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/1232712-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399130397" href="/book/show/848454.Skeleton_Crew">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1232712-matt?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1232712-matt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3552209997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer665600443247552383"><b>“I stood there for a moment, first surveying the damage, then glancing out at the mist again. It seemed closer, but it was very hard to tell for sure. If it was closer, it was defying all the laws of nature, because the wind – a very gentle breeze – was against it. That, of course, was patently impossible. It was very, very white. The only thing I can compare it to would be fresh-fallen snow lying in dazzling contrast to the deep-blue brilliance of the winter sky. But snow reflects hundreds and </b></span>
  <span id="freeText665600443247552383" style="display:none"><b>“I stood there for a moment, first surveying the damage, then glancing out at the mist again. It seemed closer, but it was very hard to tell for sure. If it was closer, it was defying all the laws of nature, because the wind – a very gentle breeze – was against it. That, of course, was patently impossible. It was very, very white. The only thing I can compare it to would be fresh-fallen snow lying in dazzling contrast to the deep-blue brilliance of the winter sky. But snow reflects hundreds and hundreds of diamond points in the sun, and this peculiar fogbank, although bright and clean-looking, did not sparkle…[M]ist isn’t uncommon on clear days, but when there’s a lot of it, the suspended moisture almost always causes a rainbow. But there was no rainbow here…”</b><br />-	Stephen King, <i>The Mist</i>, featured in <i>Skeleton Crew</i> <br /><br />When I imagine a Stephen King book in my mind, I am picturing a novel that can range in size from a brick (the mass market edition of <i>The Stand</i>) to a puppy (the hardcover edition of <i>Under the Dome</i>). I conjure memories of swollen word counts, massive backstories, and side-plot detours that can wander hundreds of pages away from the main storyline. More than anything, when I think of King’s vast body of work, I think of excess, in terms of gore, in terms of violence, in terms of sheer number of pages. And frankly, for as much as I sometimes grouse about King’s meandering tomes, that’s really what I love about him. There is something absolutely marvelous about getting entirely lost in a work such as <i>It</i>, where a simple good-evil concept is spun to lengths of which Tolstoy or Proust would have approved. <br /><br />Yet for all that, King – according to his own recollections, found in the introduction to <i>Carrie</i> – started his career writing short stories and selling them to various print magazines for a few hundred bucks a pop. He’d get an idea – invariably weird – and then bang out a draft in a few days before sending it off to publications that no longer exist. <br /><br />Normally, I don’t care much for short stories. It’s a personal taste, one that I can’t explain, except for the unsatisfied sensation of having something ending just at the point where I start becoming invested. Nevertheless, having made a small dent in King’s voluminous bibliography, I decided to check out some of his shorter works. <br /><br /><i>Skeleton Crew</i> is a collection of twenty-two short stories originally published between 1980 and 1985. Even though many of the individual selections are pretty quick, the whole shebang – cover to cover – is over five-hundred pages long. <br /><br />The headline selection in <i>Skeleton Crew</i> – and the reason I chose it in the first place – is <i>The Mist</i>. More of a novella than a short story, <i>The Mist</i> follows a group of people trapped in a supermarket after being surrounded by a fog hiding a deadly threat. It is quite good, with several top notch sequences. Still, I suggest that the movie version is vastly better, with its brutally unflinching, unforgettable ending. I suppose I couldn’t get over the fact that <i>The Mist</i> was both too long and too short. As part of a short story assemblage, it overstayed its welcome. At the same time, the concept is crackerjack, and with the potential inherent in a large cast of characters, I would have appreciated getting the full, big-novel treatment. <br /><br />Even though I was interested mainly in <i>The Mist</i>, I decided – out of compulsion, really – to read the rest of the stories straight through. As I suppose is true of any such collection, no matter how skillfully curated – and <i>Skeleton Crew</i> feels pretty random at times – it is a mixed bag. <br /><br />Surprisingly, my favorites tended to be more science-fiction than horror based. In <i>Beachworld</i>, two astronauts end up stranded on a desert planet that seems to be alive. Immediately, one of the astronauts starts going mad. Utilizing only a handful of pages, King is able to hint at a much larger – and potentially extremely interesting – universe surrounding his compact tale. In <i>The Jaunt</i>, King toys with the concepts of time, space, and teleportation, while providing a gruesome kicker of a denouement. It feels very much of a piece with <i>The Twilight Zone</i>, with the addition of King’s omnipresent willingness to take things too far. <br /><br />King has always had a warped sense of humor, and that is certainly on display in many of <i>Skeleton Crew</i>’s stories. For instance, in <i>Survivor Type</i>, a drug-running doctor ends up on a deserted island. In a series of journal entries, he narrates his increasingly extreme efforts to fend off starvation. <br /><br />Unfortunately, King also has certain unfortunate literary tricks and tics that appear and reappear so often they start to feel pathological. His handling of female characters, for instance, is extremely shaky, and often revolves around disapproving descriptions of a woman’s weight. When he’s not fat-shaming his women, King is positioning them as slutty temptresses or incessant henpeckers. A story like <i>Word Processor of the Gods</i>, about a struggling writer who has to put up with an overweight, nagging wife, simply doesn’t work anymore, if it ever worked at all. It is borderline cruel and feels like the wish fulfillment of an eternally self-centered misogynist. <br /><br />This leads to another repeated theme, that of toxic masculinity. That particular term entered the lexicon around the time that King wrote these stories, but there is no indication that he was responding to concerns about the troubling actions of certain young men. To the contrary, in <i>Skeleton Crew</i>, there are several stories in which the protagonist is an entitled male filled with murderous impulses that we are implicitly nudged to cheer. One unredeemable selection features a college student shooting people from his dorm room. (Though this was published long before Columbine, Sandy Hook, and Las Vegas, King was clearly inspired by Charles Whitman’s 1966 slaughter from atop the tower at the University of Texas-Austin). There is no point, except that it gives King the opportunity to vividly describe headshots and spattered brains. Another equally useless wallow in depravity follows an ex-college student’s vicious rampage, every murder painted with loving, leering care.<br /><br />In my experience with King, the good and bad have always gone hand-in-hand. Even his best novels have problematic parts, or sections that have aged poorly. Usually, the good outweighs the bad, often by a wide margin. <i>Skeleton Crew</i> has a closer balance. Every story is readable, and even the worst-conceived of the lot are written with King’s underrated skills. Even when the underlying framework is deplorable, most of the stories are effortlessly entertaining. They are also a bit insidious. On nights that I had read <i>Skeleton Crew</i>, I noticed that my sleep was often disrupted by vivid and unsettling dreams. That <i>Skeleton Crew</i> managed to disrupt my dream life is a compliment of sorts. <br /><br />With that said, the best stories in this assortment are not quite good enough to make you forget the rot seeping from the worst.</span>
  <a data-text-id="665600443247552383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1133829308" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1133829308" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1133829308?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399130397" href="/book/show/848454.Skeleton_Crew">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1133829308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2746875322691946938">There will be some of you that think three stars is kinda harsh for this collection. After all, it includes such amazing tales as <i>The Mist</i> and <i>The Jaunt</i>. It must be amazeballs, right? Not so much. Even the epically awesome stories in this collection need to be trimmed down. Most of them start slower than a Lars Von Trier movie, and over half of them never really pay off. There are some serious WTF stories within this collection; stories I didn't understand ten years ago and still do not understa</span>
  <span id="freeText2746875322691946938" style="display:none">There will be some of you that think three stars is kinda harsh for this collection. After all, it includes such amazing tales as <i>The Mist</i> and <i>The Jaunt</i>. It must be amazeballs, right? Not so much. Even the epically awesome stories in this collection need to be trimmed down. Most of them start slower than a Lars Von Trier movie, and over half of them never really pay off. There are some serious WTF stories within this collection; stories I didn't understand ten years ago and still do not understand today. In other words, the reread didn't help. That doesn't mean your experience will not be different. It does not mean you will not understand the Milkman stories or appreciate King's cute-ass poem about anthropomorphized fruit that he wrote for his youngest son Owen. I understand why they are in this collection, but that doesn't mean I have to like them. Mostly, this collection is tedious. But, some of the time, if you can wade through the first unmpteen pages of bullshit, you might find a scare or two, or a meaningful story surrounded by bloat. <br /><br />Here are my one-sentence reviews of each story. Feel free to discuss your favorites in the comment section.<br /><br /><i>The Mist</i> - Five epically-awesome stars for this tale of mist-borne monsters and flawed fathers.<br /> <br /><i>Here There Be Tygers</i> - Three stars for this story about toileting "tygers" and tasty teachers.<br /> <br /><i>The Monkey</i> - Two stars for this mostly mediocre, meandering monkey, because this one has never really scared me, but it sure has bored me.<br /><br /><i>Cain Rose Up</i> - Three confused stars because I don't know why this story is still in publication and <i>Rage</i> is not.<br /> <br /><i>Mrs. Todd's Shortcut</i> - Four stars for what could be the inspiration for <i>Lisey's Story</i>, because Boo'ya Moon could very well be Mrs. Todd's escape route.<br /> <br /><i>The Jaunt</i> - Five stars for this tale that takes cues from <i>The Langoliers</i>.<br /><br /><i>The Wedding Gig</i> - Four stars for this story that fits the Hard Case Crimes series better than both The <br /><i>Colorado Kid</i> and <i>Joyland</i> put together.<br /> <br /><i>Paranoid: A Chant</i> - I'm sure this piece is brilliant and I'm just too stupid to understand it, but yeah, one star.<br /> <br /><i>The Raft</i> - All the stars (Five, Six... Ten... a Hundred) for what continues to be one of my favorite stories of all time.<br /><br /><i>The Word Processor of the Gods</i> - Gets three stars for being <i>The Monkey's Paw</i> with a happy ending.<br /> <br /><i>The Man Who Would Not Shake Hands</i> - Finds three stars because the boys from 249B East 35th are still telling tales, even after Emlyn McCarron told them about <i>The Breathing Method</i>.<br /> <br /><i>Beachworld</i> - Beachfront property this ain't, but one helluva four-star story it is. <br /><br /><i>The Reaper's Image</i> - This three-star story seems like the inspiration for that horrible Oculus movie. <br /> <br /><i>Nona</i> - Gets four-stars for being darkly dubious.<br /> <br /><i>For Owen</i> - If I were King's kid I would expect something better than this two-star cutesy crap from my old man.<br /> <br /><i>Survivor Type</i> - While you'll never see Richard Pine on Food Network, his cooking gets five stars.<br /><br /><i>Uncle Otto's Truck</i> - Two stars for this done-to-death concept about a killer car.<br /> <br /><i>Morning Deliveries (Milkman #1)</i> - One star for this outline of an idea for a possible short story.<br /> <br /><i>Big Wheels: A Tale of the Laundry Game (Milkman #2)</i> - If someone would like to explain this story and its predecessor to me, I might give it more than one star.<br /><br /><i>Gramma</i> - Four-stars for this creepy motherfucker because the beginning is slow as hell, but that ending... *shivers*<br /> <br /><i>The Ballad of the Flexible Bullet</i> - This one starts even slower than Gramma but its payoff only raises it into three-star territory.<br /> <br /><i>The Reach</i> - Stephen King says he wants to be remembered for this four-star beauty of a story, but he's done much better, at least in my opinion he has.<br /><br />In summation: <i>Skeleton Crew</i> has a few gems, but is, overall, just okay. <br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: I'd rather take a jaunt on a raft through the mist.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2746875322691946938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2823738892" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2823738892" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2823738892?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28378571-skeleton-crew">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2823738892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer998390326753020049"><i>You can find <a href='http://novelnotions.net/2019/06/03/skeleton-crew/' rel='nofollow noopener'>this</a> review and more at <a href='http://novelnotions.net' rel='nofollow noopener'>Novel Notions</a>. </i><br/><br/>Stephen King is such a master storyteller. I’ve come to love him over the past few years, and I now count him among my favorite authors. I have to agree with the masses, however; King tends to fall flat when it comes to endings. Thankfully, that’s not really an issue when it comes to short stories. They’re not supposed to really end, which I think is a huge boon in King’s favor. As with Night Shift, the first of King’s short story collections I</span>
  <span id="freeText998390326753020049" style="display:none"><i>You can find <a href="http://novelnotions.net/2019/06/03/skeleton-crew/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> review and more at <a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a>. </i><br /><br />Stephen King is such a master storyteller. I’ve come to love him over the past few years, and I now count him among my favorite authors. I have to agree with the masses, however; King tends to fall flat when it comes to endings. Thankfully, that’s not really an issue when it comes to short stories. They’re not supposed to really end, which I think is a huge boon in King’s favor. As with Night Shift, the first of King’s short story collections I read, Skeleton Crew was chockfull of the interesting, terrifying, and uncomfortable. While not every story was a resounding success, there were far more hits among these twenty two installments than there were misses, and a handful of these stories will be staying with me for a good long while.<br /><br />The first selection in this collection is one of King’s novellas, The Mist, my review of which you can read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2733291309?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>. Beyond that, the stories that resonated the most with me were The Monkey, The Jaunt, Word Processor of the Gods, Nona, Survivor Type, The Ballad of the Flexible Bullet, Gramma, and The Reach. All of these stories I would have rated anywhere from 4 to 5 stars, which I think is a pretty high percentage for a short story collection. Some of these story were scary, while others were merely uncomfortable. Only one story actually gave me nightmares, and that was a tale of self-cannibalism that included not a single supernatural element. It was absolutely horrifying. Then there’s The Reach, which was a poignant way to close out the collection. Also, there were a handful of Castle Rock stories, which is always fun to come across if you’re one of King’s Constant Readers, which I’m beginning to consider myself. One thing that I think King should steer clear of though is poetry. There were two poems in this collection and they just didn’t land.<br /><br />If you’ve never read Stephen King and would like to give his work a try, I cannot suggest highly enough picking up one of his short story collections. You’ll get a taste for his style, and there’s something about King’s storytelling in short form that I find a good deal scarier than some of his novels. Whether he’s spinning a tale that spans a dozen pages or more than a thousand, King is undoubtably the master of the horror genre, at least in my eyes. Long live the King!</span>
  <a data-text-id="998390326753020049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The six stories I loved are probably some of my favorite Stephen King stories but the rest were just blah! <br/><br/>The Good: <br/>1)The Raft is my favorite story in this collection.   <span id="freeText2394563531549577119" style="display:none">Skeleton Crew is my least favorite Stephen King story collection. Its not a bad collection, but something just felt off. The six stories I loved are probably some of my favorite Stephen King stories but the rest were just blah! <br /><br />The Good: <br />1)The Raft is my favorite story in this collection. A group of friends on a raft find themselves being picked off by some mysterious black slug in the water.<br />2)Word Processor of the Gods. A man who hates his life discovers he can delete or add people and things in his life through his new Word Processor. <br />3)The Reapers Image is one of King's best stories period. As someone who actually has seen an inexplicable image in a mirror, I love scary stories involving mirrors. <br />4)Survivor Type is so disturbing that while I loved it, I will never read it again. A surgeon is stranded on a island and finds that one particular meat is tastier than the rest. <br />5)Uncle Otto's Truck, Stephen King loves a haunted car and I think this story is best of all of his haunted car stories. <br />6) Gramma I've heard or read this story before but I can't remember where. Gramma never dies. <br /><br />I'm not going to go into detail on the bottom 3 because I just don't care enough. <br />The Mist was a disappointment because I had such high hopes.<br /> The Wedding Gift was pointless and not funny in the least.<br />Beachworld was boring. <br /><br />Skeleton Crew is a good collection but with Stephen King I've come to expect greatness. If you love Stephen King I would still recommend this but for the casual King reader maybe skip it.<br /><br />Hooked On Books September Read-A-Thon</span>

<div id="review_3587813410" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3587813410" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3587813410?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399130397" href="/book/show/848454.Skeleton_Crew">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3587813410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17171034665389800800">Some of Stephen King's most impressive work often appears in the form of his short stories. It's almost a given that in any anthology of his, there'll at least be some stories that I can appreciate and admire, as is the case with his enormous 1980's anthology <i>Skeleton Crew</i>, which features an image depicting a hideous monkey on the front cover. <i>Skeleton Crew</i> is interesting in that it blends a good mix of sci-fi, fantasy and horror all into one, and most of the stories in the book are still releva</span>
  <span id="freeText17171034665389800800" style="display:none">Some of Stephen King's most impressive work often appears in the form of his short stories. It's almost a given that in any anthology of his, there'll at least be some stories that I can appreciate and admire, as is the case with his enormous 1980's anthology <i>Skeleton Crew</i>, which features an image depicting a hideous monkey on the front cover. <i>Skeleton Crew</i> is interesting in that it blends a good mix of sci-fi, fantasy and horror all into one, and most of the stories in the book are still relevant to some extent even today. While not as unique as <i>Night Shift</i>, <i>Skeleton Crew</i> still contains a few memorable and very well-written works.<br /><br />Some of my favourite ones included "Morning Deliveries" (featuring a lecherous, creepy milkman with some nasty tricks up his sleeve), "Word Processor of the Gods", which was adapted into a <i>Tales from the Darkside</i> episode in the 1980's (I still have a copy of it with the original VHS tape soundtrack), the somewhat comedic "Here There Be Tygers" that anybody who's ever been a kid in school will get a laugh out of, "Gramma" (really weird but a good one), and "The Wedding Gig", which was a bit convoluted but still interesting).<br /><br />There were a few that just weren't for me, mostly the sci-fi ones, and especially the stories which had very vague, unresolved endings. There is one story in particular called "The Raft" where most of the characters are wholly unlikable and where their never-ending bizarre decisions just don't make much sense. "The Mist", which inspired the 2007 feature film and the later TV miniseries filmed right here in the Bedford Mall where I go to eat at Swiss Chalet and used to shop at Target (now vacant, hence why it served as the set for the miniseries), is a decent story but somewhat aimless and not very original, considering similar apocalyptic stories from the time period in which it was written. <br /><br />Overall, <i>Skeleton Crew</i> has a lot of short stories that I really enjoyed, and a lot that I didn't get much out of, but it's a good King anthology with some better examples of his short story work. Fans of <i>Tales from the Darkside</i> and <i>The Twilight Zone</i> will probably like reading the stories that inspired certain episodes, and King as always offers a kind of reflection of the fears of contemporary American society, still ringing true all these years later. Caring for a difficult relative, science being explored with no boundaries or ethics, the figures we welcome into our safe, suburban neighbourhoods, among other things. This is an anthology I'd recommend to any King fan, although it isn't my favourite anthology of his.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17171034665389800800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1689238393?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ron" href="/user/show/43881851-ron">Ron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=short-story">short-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=anthology-collection">anthology-collection</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1689238393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1527328557924216038"><b>Skeleton Crew.</b> What a great name for this book of short stories. Many pack a scare. Some not so much. I thought I’d just highlight a few of my favorites:<br/><br/><b>The Mist</b> - It’s by far the longest “short story” in the collection. Really, it could be called a novella. I’m glad it was included here instead of a novella collection (something that SK has become famous for doing). The Mist starts things off with a bang, or should I say a storm. After the storm comes the mist, and within that mist is the stuff</span>
  <span id="freeText1527328557924216038" style="display:none"><b>Skeleton Crew.</b> What a great name for this book of short stories. Many pack a scare. Some not so much. I thought I’d just highlight a few of my favorites:<br /><br /><b>The Mist</b> - It’s by far the longest “short story” in the collection. Really, it could be called a novella. I’m glad it was included here instead of a novella collection (something that SK has become famous for doing). The Mist starts things off with a bang, or should I say a storm. After the storm comes the mist, and within that mist is the stuff of children’s nightmares. A crowd of people end up in turmoil together against that stuff, and at first there’s only a feeling that something terrible is hidden in the mist. Call it the calm before the shit hits the fan. At this point SK explores some of the characters involved. It’s just what I love to see, and here I am pleasantly reminded of a few of SK’s other full length novels. The Mist is just long enough to glimpse some personalities. Enough to get me invested even a second time around.<br /><b>The Monkey</b> - Holy shit did this toy monkey ever sell from the store’s shelf again after this story? And for those who already owned one think about it lying inside a box in the upstairs attic, eyes wide open, cymbals poised? This scary good story may be the reason I never owned one myself.<br /><b>The Raft</b> - The title alone sets your mind to wondering. A raft. Water. Isolation. King’s imagination takes you beyond the norm. Give me a shark to contend with. I want off this raft. And what could be the most terrifying part of this story, is that fact that I felt like the fifth person on that raft, just trying to figure a way to shore.<br /><b>Word Processor of the Gods</b> - This is so good because it is the reimagining of the genie in the bottle, or “The Monkey’s Paw” by WW Jacobs. Again, it became the question of “What would I do?”, while at the same time telling its main character to STOP, or at least SLOW DOWN because I need time to think first. Fun and thrilling.<br /><b>The Reaper’s Image</b> - An antique mirror, or looking-glass as it was called, is locked away in the attic for a good reason. Some people cannot help themselves. Maybe that’s because it’s priceless, or maybe something else. The story is short, and seems to have been purposely written with little crisis, but then end gets me all the same.<br /><b>Survivor Type</b> - This one proved that it’s possible to hate the protagonist yet still love the story. For me, that is a rarity. Maybe that’s what King set out to do. Provide a desperate situation that keeps the reader riveted and place a dirtball in the center of it. I don’t know. The shock value counts for a lot here, and I wonder, “Would I like the story even more with a character I cared for, or less?”<br /><b>The Ballad of the Flexible Bullet</b> - Again, what a great title. It’s the Crew’s second longest story. Not it’s best. Much of the first three-fourths succumb to a slow pace. All I can say is you got to make it through to the end because that’s where the payoff occurs. Saved by a great finale.<br /><br />King includes a nice afterward, at least in the 1985 HC edition, in what he calls such things that might interest the casual reader. He includes a few notes for a few of the stories describing how each came about. I love a peak into his mind. Even SK is stumped for an idea at times, but then a most mundane experience occurs, and a story is born from real life.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1527328557924216038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1002290744" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1002290744" />
    <a title="Joe Valdez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez"><img alt="Joe Valdez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585885999p2/26876584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1002290744?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe Valdez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe Valdez" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez">Joe Valdez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399130397" href="/book/show/848454.Skeleton_Crew">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26876584-joe-valdez?shelf=anthology">anthology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26876584-joe-valdez?shelf=paranormal-general">paranormal-general</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1002290744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3602981395733406057">Revisiting <i>Skeleton Crew</i>, Stephen King's collection of twenty-two short stories published in 1985, for the first time since I was in 7th grade -- a time when I was trying to dress like Don Johnson and get Madonna's "Into the Groove" out of my head -- was a wonderful experience. The horror stories I loved as a 12-year-old were each better than I remember. A couple I didn't have the patience for back then became new discoveries. A lot of the stories I never cottoned to are still terrible. <br/><br/>Five sta</span>
  <span id="freeText3602981395733406057" style="display:none">Revisiting <i>Skeleton Crew</i>, Stephen King's collection of twenty-two short stories published in 1985, for the first time since I was in 7th grade -- a time when I was trying to dress like Don Johnson and get Madonna's "Into the Groove" out of my head -- was a wonderful experience. The horror stories I loved as a 12-year-old were each better than I remember. A couple I didn't have the patience for back then became new discoveries. A lot of the stories I never cottoned to are still terrible. <br /><br />Five stars:<br /><br /><i>The Mist</i>. This novella of apocalyptic doom and ravenous monsters at the threshold may be the most terrifying thing I've ever read. Imaginative and horrible, <i>The Alamo</i> meets H.P. Lovecraft, I've reread certain passages to make sure I read what I imagined I did. King's depiction of how quickly good folk descend into a mob when confronted by their own mortality is one of his finest pieces ever. I've never looked at supermarkets the same way again.<br /><br /><i>Mrs. Todd's Shortcut</i>. One of the stories I skipped at age 12. No monsters, no boogeymen, but love stuff? Gross! King's creativity bloomed for me this time around, as did his unabashed romance for Ophelia Todd, one of the more compelling characters in what usually amounts to a rogue's gallery for him.<br /><br /><i>The Jaunt</i>. Spellbinding science fiction tale that documents the invention of teleportation (in 1987!) and how a family preparing for a jaunt to Mars hundreds of years later comes out the other end with a valuable lesson about space-time travel. This one still blows my mind.<br /><br /><i>The Raft</i>. Another one of King's most primal and terrifying tales. In a lot of King's stories, I can imagine myself getting out of the predicament with logic and abundant knowledge of horror movie cliches, but this is one story I want no participation in whatsoever.<br /><br /><i>Uncle Otto's Truck</i>. This was another story I skipped over when I was younger. Since, I've come to appreciate a great yarn. Everyone has a story to tell and I can hardly resist a first-person account by a character who seems to be whispering to the reader that they have something they really want to get off their chest, something we might not believe, but really happened.<br /><br />Four stars:<br /><br /><i>The Monkey</i>. Not quite as scary as I remember it, but still wonderfully written. A windup monkey with crashing cymbals doesn't quite scare me, but the journey the protagonist takes from orphaned boy to adult and his battle with this evil thing is compelling.<br /><br /><i>Nona</i>. Bumpy at the beginning, this is another terrific yarn, a jailhouse confessional by a convicted killer whose account of his raven haired, irresistible accomplice cannot be verified by any witness. It's quite creepy. The tie-in to <i>The Body</i> was an unexpected treat.<br /><br /><i>Survivor Type</i>. Not terribly suspenseful, more of a gross-out story, but the lengths King goes to describe how a rogue doctor ended up marooned with surgical equipment and heroin is imaginative as hell. <br /><br />The other stories range from decent (<i>The Reaper's Image</i>, <i>Word Processor of the Gods</i>) to godawful messes (I can't even begin to unravel what the hell is going on in <i>Milkman #1</i> or <i>Milkman #2</i>. I now remember why after <i>The Raft</i>, why <i>Skeleton Crew</i> becomes something of a chore to power through and finish. There's junk mixed amid the treasures, but part of the fun was dumpster diving here and discovering that for myself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3602981395733406057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau"><img alt="Ashley Daviau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599784716p2/35915119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_1745267978" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1745267978" />
    <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf"><img alt="Cody | CodysBookshelf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592500568p2/56352820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1745267978?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cody | CodysBookshelf" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf">Cody | CodysBookshelf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399130397" href="/book/show/848454.Skeleton_Crew">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf?shelf=halloween-reading-2016">halloween-reading-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1745267978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13508795244510830694">I finished Skeleton Crew with tears in my eyes. I thought I'd read "The Reach" — the story that closes out this collection — before, but I guess I hadn't. It was an entirely new experience for me, and it packed quite the emotional wallop. As I write this review I'm still trying to mentally recover from that one, so pardon me if my thoughts are a little scattered. My Fornit died, and I'm stuck doing the job myself.<br/> <br/>By the time this collection was published in 1985, Stephen King was a bona-fide li</span>
  <span id="freeText13508795244510830694" style="display:none">I finished Skeleton Crew with tears in my eyes. I thought I'd read "The Reach" — the story that closes out this collection — before, but I guess I hadn't. It was an entirely new experience for me, and it packed quite the emotional wallop. As I write this review I'm still trying to mentally recover from that one, so pardon me if my thoughts are a little scattered. My Fornit died, and I'm stuck doing the job myself.<br /> <br />By the time this collection was published in 1985, Stephen King was a bona-fide literary rock star. His fame was gargantuan, beaten in size only by his addiction to dope and alcohol. According to the man himself, his study was the site of nightly parties for one, where the beer flowed and nose candy was always available. Yeah, King wasn't in a great state of mind for most of the eighties. He warns the reader in this book's introduction that the act of writing short stories hadn't gotten easier for him over the years — instead, it had gotten harder. Novel deadlines made it difficult to carve out time for shorter tales, and everything the man put into his Word Processor of the Gods wanted to be six hundred pages in length. If this reviewer is being honest, that's painfully apparent with this collection. A handful of the tales presented here should've never made it off the cutting room floor and several others could have been trimmed a bit. Most of what the reader is presented with is great (hence the four stars), but King overwrites like crazy here. That's my problem with a lot of his output from this decade — excess verbosity.<br /> <br /><br /> <br />After the reliably folksy, mood-setting introduction to this collection from Sai King himself, things get rolling with "The Mist," the first (but not last) story in Skeleton Crew about ordinary people stranded and facing likely death, due to out-of-this-world circumstances. "The Mist" is a novella, and I always enjoy every word of it. Yeah, King overwrites in several places in this book . . . but this story ain't one of 'em. I have quite the fear of mist, thanks to this story. Other favorites of mine include "The Ballad Of The Flexible Bullet," a delightfully paranoid story King could have never written before or after cocaine; "The Raft," which was my very favorite in this collection for a long time; The Monkey," a story that doesn't get as much love as it deserves; "The Reach," the previously mentioned story that moved me to tears; "The Jaunt," which, for my money, contains King's most haunting story ending yet; and "Cain Rose Up," a story that other reviewers like to rag on but I can't help but dig.<br /> <br /><br /> <br />All that said, there are several stories here that should have gotten canned. "Here There Be Tygers" makes no sense and is downright gimmicky; the two "Milkman" stories also don't make much sense and go nowhere. "Uncle Otto's Truck," a story about (you guessed it) a haunted truck, feels worn out and old — King has touched on this theme so many times in his career. I also don't like "For Owen" at all, and "Paranoid: A Chant" should have been folded into "The Ballad Of The Flexible Bullet" where it belongs. It's a shame this collection is somewhat weighed down by so many DOA entries, because there are several genuine classics here. This one just isn't very consistent, and if that's what you're looking for might I recommend Night Shift or Just After Sunset?<br /> <br />All in all, this is very much a collection worth checking out. It was released during King's "classic" period, so of course it's worth a purchase. The theme of external isolation and humanity's will to save itself is done really well in "The Mist," "Beachworld," "Survivor Type," and "The Raft." I also like this book's "Do you love?" motif — it makes this collection hang together much better than it probably should. This is definitely a strong read, and I will come back to my favorites for years to come.<br /> <br /><br /> <br />King connections:<br /> <br />(I tried to take actual notes for this one, as I knew there are connections to the King universe all over the place. I know I missed some, but here's what I caught while reading. Sorry my notes are a little scattered.)<br /> <br />"The Mist"<br /> <br />P. 94 - David Clayton, our main character, thinks of a character as "looking like a crazy gunslinger in an existential comedy."<br />It is theorized that The Shop is at least partially responsible for the mist. I could totally see that. <br />I'm not sure if this is a connection or not, but when David and a few others make the courageous trek to the pharmacy next door, they encounter an "otherworldly" presence that takes the shape of a spider . . . though they know it's something more. Any relation to IT? Totally possible, as that book was published the following year. <br /> <br />"Mrs. Todd's Shortcut"<br /> <br />It takes place in Castle Rock, home of several King novels and short stories.<br />P. 182 - Joe Camber of Cujo is mentioned.<br />P. 186 - Haven gets a shout out!<br /> <br />"The Man Who Would Not Shake Hands"<br /> <br />This one could be could be seen as a spiritual successor to "The Breathing Method," even going so far as to reference that earlier novella. It revoles around the same, strange story-telling club that we first met in Different Seasons. <br /> <br />"Nona"<br /> <br />It takes place in Castle Rock, firmly placing it in the same universe as "Mrs. Todd's Shortcut" as well as several other King stories.<br />The narrator of "Nona" mentions once getting "messed up" by Ace Merrill, the local baddie — an antagonist in "The Body" and Needful Things.<br />The narrator lets the reader know he grew up in Harlow, Maine — the setting of "N." and Revival.<br />P. 347 — Vern Tessio of "The Body" gets a brief mention. Cool!<br /> <br />"Uncle Otto's Truck"<br /> <br />Both Derry and Castle Rock play an important role in this one. <br /> <br /> <br />"Gramma"<br /> <br />P. 421 - Cora Simard and Henrietta Dodd are mentioned. George, the protagonist in "Gramma," listens to one of the ladies' phone conversations on a party line. Cora's daughter, Rhonda, was a student of Ewen High School and was among Carrie White's tormentors. Henrietta Dodd was the mother of Frank Dodd, as seen in The Dead Zone and mentioned in various other Castle Rock stories.<br />Joe Camber gets another mention! This story takes place near Castle Rock in 1977-ish (I think), so before the major events of Carrie and Cujo. Hmm.<br /> <br />Favorite story: <br /> <br />"The Ballad Of The Flexible Bullet" <br /> <br />Least favorite story:<br /> <br />"Big Wheels: A Tale Of The Laundry Game (Milkman #2)"<br /> <br />Favorite quote: <br /> <br />“I sit on the bench in front of Bell's Market and think about Homer Buckland and about the beautiful girl who leaned over to open his door when he come down that path with the full red gasoline can in his right hand - she looked like a girl of no more than sixteen, a girl on her learner's permit, and her beauty was terrible, but I believe it would no longer kill the man it turned itself on; for a moment her eyes lit on me, I was not killed, although a part of me died at her feet."<br />(from "Mrs. Todd's Shortcut") <br /> <br />Up next: <br /> <br />It's everything you ever were afraid of. It's . . . IT. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13508795244510830694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2327195321" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2327195321" />
    <a title="Jamie Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15954768-jamie-stewart"><img alt="Jamie Stewart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551013124p2/15954768.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2327195321?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie Stewart" href="/user/show/15954768-jamie-stewart">Jamie Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2327195321&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2327195321" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer911644062233169802">While Skeleton Crew overall doesn’t reach the heights of Stephen King’s previous collection for me, it still contains some fantastically brilliant stories. I found when I was reading Skeleton Crew that the stories within it could be split into three different categories. The first category is something I thought of as pedal-to-the-floor King were the story has no fat or tangents and is all go, go, GO!. The second category I thought of as being for folksy tales that tend to go off on tangents, an</span>
  <span id="freeText911644062233169802" style="display:none">While Skeleton Crew overall doesn’t reach the heights of Stephen King’s previous collection for me, it still contains some fantastically brilliant stories. I found when I was reading Skeleton Crew that the stories within it could be split into three different categories. The first category is something I thought of as pedal-to-the-floor King were the story has no fat or tangents and is all go, go, GO!. The second category I thought of as being for folksy tales that tend to go off on tangents, and the third category I thought of when encountering stories that held weirdness and had an overall surreal feel. With these in mind let the rating begin. <br /><br />The Mist - 5 Stars - The Mist is really a novella and its the first incidence of pedal-to-the-floor King. Even though this story is the longest in the collection it does not feel long at all when reading it, which is a clear indicator of how good it is. I always think the best stories are ones that make you want to swallow them whole on the first read and leave you wanting to reread instantly. That's exactly what The Mist did for me. It's a simple story about a father, his son and their obnoxious neighbour as they drive to the local supermarket after a storm in rural Maine and become trapped inside by a mysterious mist. There's something in the mist, in fact, we learn that there are multiple things in the mist, but we only get glimpses of some of them. Its all left to our imaginations in the same way the creation of this mist is. There are references to a secret government project close to this community where the characters live, but nothing is ever confirmed, instead, the characters just have to react. And it's those reactions, which pass by at breakneck speed, that keep the reader invested as each character has their own way of dealing with this disaster. <br /> <br />Here There Be Typers - 3 Stars - This story falls into the third category. A young boy is given permission to use the restroom at school by his cruel teacher only to discover a tiger in the bathroom. Weird. <br /><br />The Monkey - 3.5 Stars - This uses a narrative device that King would later perfect in writing It. The reader gets two stories, one from the perspective of a child and another after that child has entered into middle age. <br /><br />Cain Rose Up - 2 Stars - With so many school shootings it makes this story a difficult read. <br /><br />Mrs. Todd Shortcut - 3 Stars - A lot of people seem to really like this story and I can understand why. It falls into the folksy category and for a lot of people these types of stories rely on you falling for the characters within them. I didn't. I still found the premise interesting, about a woman who discovers short cuts that allow her to travel to places quickly even when it verges on the physically impossible. Plus, the hinted explanation is linked to themes King has explored in other stories such as a multiverse is a nice side story but it didn't not me over. <br /><br />The Jaunt - 4 Stars - The possibilities within this short story are endless. Plus, it features one of the creepiest lines of dialogue in any King story. <br /><br />The Wedding Gig - 1 Stars - A didn't really see the point of this story, plus its depiction of people that are overweight and race makes me uncomfortable. <br /><br />The Raft - 5 Stars - Like The Mist this one has its foot to the floor. It's a simple tale about four teens that head to a lake only to fall victim to a monster. What more could you want? The body horror here is some of King's best. <br /><br />Word Processor of the Gods - 4 Stars - A trashy story due to certain characters but it holds plenty of charm.<br /><br />The Man Who Would Not Shake Hands - 3 Stars - An interesting tale from King as it’s a return to a location from another story, The Breathing Method. In it men tell stories to one another, stories of horror and magic. It’s an enjoyable read as it provides King the chance to write in a different style similarly to Victorian mysterious. <br /><br />Beachworld- 4 Stars - A story about two astronauts who crash land on a desert planet. Chilling and atmospheric, this one of the collection most memorable tales. <br /><br />The Reaper’s Image - 4 Stars - This one had a very Night Shift vibe for me. <br /><br />Nona - 4.5 Stars - Reminded me of Strawberry Spring from Night Shift. <br /><br />Survivor Type - 5 Stars - I haven’t read this story in years and I remember it having a real lasting affect on me as a teenager. I’m happy to say it still lives up to my memory of this horrifying, gruesome tale. It’s one of King’s finest and like the best ones in this collection has very little fat in it. It also reminds me of a section in the early Resident Evil games were the gamer finds a diary with a similar story in it. <br /><br />Uncle Otto’s Truck - 3 Stars - Another folksy tale told in first person. <br /><br />Morning Deliveries (Milkman#1) - 4 Stars - A story that has an interesting premise but is too short. I wanted more! <br /><br />Big Wheels: A Tale of the Laundry Game (Milkman#2) - 2 Stars - This story has little to do with the previous one and is as long and rambling as the drunken stories it’s characters tell. It’s my least favourite story in the collection.<br /><br />Gramma - 4.5 Stars - This one creepy, chilling and hair raising tale about a young boy having to be alone in his house with his sick Gramma. That ending!! Damn did it deliver. <br /><br />The Ballad of the Flexible Bullet - 4 Stars - This is an interesting story that reflects on how certain people develop habits and mental tics while contemplating the idea of what happens when a person’s mind becomes self-destructive. It’s lengthy and it is a story that is told by someone about someone else and while that didn’t necessarily work for in me with Mrs. Todd’s Shortcut, it worked me here. I found myself being pulled into the story by the narrators' voice. <br /><br />The Reach - 3 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="911644062233169802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kerri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51649609-kerri"><img alt="Kerri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573956228p2/51649609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1514495685?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kerri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kerri" href="/user/show/51649609-kerri">Kerri</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer395908606316984717">I thoroughly enjoyed this short story collection. I made a few notes about some of the stories:<br/><br/>- The Mist<br/>Brilliant. Really want to see the movie version, and check out the audio version that Scott mentions in the comments! <br/><br/>- The Monkey <br/>Particularly creepy. I found this uncomfortably believable! Anything with ominous toys/dolls tends to get under my skin.<br/><br/>- Mrs Todd's Shortcut <br/>Quite beautiful -- loved it with an unexpected intensity. <br/><br/>- The Raft<br/>I hate LaVerne so much. She's that female character th</span>
  <span id="freeText395908606316984717" style="display:none">I thoroughly enjoyed this short story collection. I made a few notes about some of the stories:<br /><br />- The Mist<br />Brilliant. Really want to see the movie version, and check out the audio version that Scott mentions in the comments! <br /><br />- The Monkey <br />Particularly creepy. I found this uncomfortably believable! Anything with ominous toys/dolls tends to get under my skin.<br /><br />- Mrs Todd's Shortcut <br />Quite beautiful -- loved it with an unexpected intensity. <br /><br />- The Raft<br />I hate LaVerne so much. She's that female character that's so often present in books/movies especially horror. The kind of character where, terrible as it may sound, I feel pleased when someone finally hits her (if it was a real life situation I would NOT feel that way, but this is fictional, and in the realms of fiction my moral compass is different).<br /> I've been thinking about my intense dislike of her, and those of her ilk, the vapid airheads who do nothing but scream hysterically or swoon pathetically, and I have concluded that some of it stems from a worry that if I found myself in such a situation, I might react the same. No stoicism or being calm and collected, just a blubbering mess! I dislike that possibility, so I intensely dislike the characters that represent that. Also, they tend to be excruciatingly annoying. <br /> In 'The Mist' when the (less annoying) Amanda, 'screamed ceaselessly, like a firebell', Mrs. Reppler says, "Woman, shut your head" --- and I loved her in that moment! I hope I would be a Mrs. Reppler, rather than an Amanda or, returning to this story, a LaVerne. I do feel sorry for her though, considering the situation she found herself in.<br /><br />- Word Processor of the Gods<br />Loved this one! I admit Googling a picture of a word processor, so I had a better image of the technology. I've never seen one before. A little before my time I suppose. I really liked the outcome of this one too -- unexpected. <br /><br />- Survivor Type<br />I winced constantly while I read this. It's stuck in my head and I'd prefer that it wasn't! <br /><br />- Gramma <br />This one scared me! Something I really find interesting is coming across as story that scares you more you'd have thought. This one just got to me, and from the blurb it didn't sound that bad -- but it was! <br /><br />- The Ballad of the Flexible Bullet <br />'Madness is a flexible bullet.'<br /> Probably my favourite in this collection.</span>
  <a data-text-id="395908606316984717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1118969399" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1118969399" />
    <a title="B Schrodinger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5448792-b-schrodinger"><img alt="B Schrodinger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572325701p2/5448792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1118969399?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B Schrodinger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B Schrodinger" href="/user/show/5448792-b-schrodinger">B Schrodinger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340952627" href="/book/show/848452.Skeleton_Crew">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5448792-b-schrodinger?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5448792-b-schrodinger?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1118969399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2210604896185157473">Stephen King seems to be a bit hit and miss with me. Sometimes there can be a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13596166.Joyland' title='Joyland by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Joyland</a> and sometimes there can be a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6320534.Under_the_Dome' title='Under the Dome by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Under the Dome</a>. But they have never been bad or unreadable, just seemingly poor, rushed and formulaic. I am noticing that I like his more modern tales greater than his 80s and 90s huge output.<br/><br/>So here is a short story collection from that time. The time where it seems like he was writing a book every couple of months. And it was just how I find myself feeling about all of his works. </span>
  <span id="freeText2210604896185157473" style="display:none">Stephen King seems to be a bit hit and miss with me. Sometimes there can be a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13596166.Joyland" title="Joyland by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Joyland</a> and sometimes there can be a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6320534.Under_the_Dome" title="Under the Dome by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Under the Dome</a>. But they have never been bad or unreadable, just seemingly poor, rushed and formulaic. I am noticing that I like his more modern tales greater than his 80s and 90s huge output.<br /><br />So here is a short story collection from that time. The time where it seems like he was writing a book every couple of months. And it was just how I find myself feeling about all of his works. There were some hits, but there were also some misses.<br /><br />The great tales here were:- <br /><br />'The Mist' as post-apocalyptic Cthulhu tale that is very suspenseful, but a little dated now. But still a good deal of fun.<br /><br />'The Monkey' which I am sure has kind of entered into horror as a classic. A toy monkey that taunts and sticks around more than it's welcome.<br /><br />'Mrs Todd's Shortcut' should delight any map nerd or even mathematicians. Very clever.<br /><br />'Uncle Otto's Truck' mirrors 'The Monkey' and even "Christine' which I have not read yet.<br /><br />'Gramma' is great and haunting. What do you do with your dead Gramma?<br /><br />But while these stand out others were just OK. But there was one or two ones that did annoy me. Especially 'The Jaunt' which seems to be Stephen's attempt at traditional SF short story writing. It was terrible. It brings back memories of the last section of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23356529.11_23_63" title="11 23 63 by Steven King" rel="nofollow noopener">11 23 63</a>. He cannot do SF. But still I'm hoping that this statement is wrong.<br /><br />So a great read for fans and a recommendation to casual readers. You might not love everything here, but there is a good chunk of it to love.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2210604896185157473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
